To enforce that no two equal instances\n/// are created, Type instances can only be created via static factory methods\n/// in class Type and in derived classes.  Once allocated, Types are never\n/// free'd.\n///\nclass Type {\npublic:\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  /// Definitions of all of the base types for the Type system.  Based on this\n  /// value, you can cast to a class defined in DerivedTypes.h.\n  /// Note: If you add an element to this, you need to add an element to the\n  /// Type::getPrimitiveType function, or else things will break!\n  /// Also update LLVMTypeKind and LLVMGetTypeKind () in the C binding.\n  ///\n  enum TypeID {\n    // PrimitiveTypes\n    HalfTyID = 0,  ///< 16-bit floating point type\n    BFloatTyID,    ///< 16-bit floating point type (7-bit significand)\n    FloatTyID,     ///< 32-bit floating point type\n    DoubleTyID,    ///< 64-bit floating point type\n    X86_FP80TyID,  ///< 80-bit floating point type (X87)\n    FP128TyID,     ///< 128-bit floating point type (112-bit significand)\n    PPC_FP128TyID, ///< 128-bit floating point type (two 64-bits, PowerPC)\n    VoidTyID,      ///< type with no size\n    LabelTyID,     ///< Labels\n    MetadataTyID,  ///< Metadata\n    X86_AMXTyID,   ///< AMX vectors (8192 bits, X86 specific)\n    TokenTyID,     ///< Tokens\n\n    // Derived types... see DerivedTypes.h file.\n    IntegerTyID,        ///< Arbitrary bit width integers\n    FunctionTyID,       ///< Functions\n    PointerTyID,        ///< Pointers\n    StructTyID,         ///< Structures\n    ArrayTyID,          ///< Arrays\n    FixedVectorTyID,    ///< Fixed width SIMD vector type\n    ScalableVectorTyID, ///< Scalable SIMD vector type\n    TypedPointerTyID,   ///< Typed pointer used by some GPU targets\n    TargetExtTyID,      ///< Target extension type\n  };\n\nprivate:\n  /// This refers to the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n  LLVMContext &Context;\n\n  TypeID   ID : 8;            // The current base type of this type.\n  unsigned SubclassData : 24; // Space for subclasses to store data.\n                              // Note that this should be synchronized with\n                              // MAX_INT_BITS value in IntegerType class.\n\nprotected:\n  friend class LLVMContextImpl;\n\n  explicit Type(LLVMContext &C, TypeID tid)\n    : Context(C), ID(tid), SubclassData(0) {}\n  ~Type() = default;\n\n  unsigned getSubclassData() const { return SubclassData; SelectionDAG type legalization can require a\n    57→      ///< power of 2 IntegerType, so limit to the largest representable power\n    58→      ///< of 2, 8388608.\n    59→  };\n    60→\n    61→  /// This static method is the primary way of constructing an IntegerType.\n    62→  /// If an IntegerType with the same NumBits value was previously instantiated,\n    63→  /// that instance will be returned. Otherwise a new one will be created. As each created node gets a\n  // new id we do not need to worry about reuse expunging.  Should we\n  // run out of ids, we can do a one time expensive compactifcation.\n  typedef unsigned TableId;\n\n  TableId NextValueId = 1;\n\n  SmallDenseMap<SDValue, TableId, 8> ValueToIdMap;\n TableId, 8> PromotedFloats;\n\n  /// For floating-point nodes that have a smaller precision than the smallest\n  /// supported precision, this map indicates the converted value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> SoftPromotedHalfs;\n\n  /// For float nodes that need to be expanded this map indicates which operands\n  /// are the expanded version of the input.\n TableId, 8> ScalarizedVectors;\n\n  /// For nodes that need to be split this map indicates which operands are the\n  /// expanded version of the input.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, std::pair<TableId, TableId>, 8> SplitVectors;\n\n  /// For vector nodes that need to be widened, indicates the widened value to\n  /// use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> WidenedVectors;\n\n  /// For values that {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01SMbdPa5zsSK4Zw5Hagkoau","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→//===-- LegalizeTypes.cpp - Common code for DAG type legalizer ------------===//\n     2→//\n     3→// Part of the LLVM Project, under the Apache License v2.0 with LLVM Exceptions.\n     4→// See https://llvm.org/LICENSE.txt for license information.\n     5→// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 WITH LLVM-exception\n     6→//\n     7→//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n     8→//\n     9→// This file implements the SelectionDAG::LegalizeTypes method.  It transforms\n    10→// an arbitrary well-formed SelectionDAG to only consist of legal types.  This\n    11→// is common code shared among the LegalizeTypes*.cpp files.\n    12→//\n    13→//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n    14→\n    15→#include \"LegalizeTypes.h\"\n    16→#include \"llvm/ADT/SetVector.h\"\n    17→#include \"llvm/IR/DataLayout.h\"\n    18→#include \"llvm/Support/CommandLine.h\"\n    19→#include \"llvm/Support/ErrorHandling.h\"\n    20→#include \"llvm/Support/raw_ostream.h\"\n    21→using namespace llvm;\n    22→\n    23→#define DEBUG_TYPE \"legalize-types\"\n    24→\n    25→static cl::opt<bool>\n    26→EnableExpensiveChecks(\"enable-legalize-types-checking\", cl::Hidden);\n    27→\n    28→/// Do extensive, expensive, basic correctness checking.\n    29→void DAGTypeLegalizer::PerformExpensiveChecks() {\n    30→  // If a node is not processed, then none of its values should be mapped by any\n    31→  // of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\n    32→\n    33→  // If a node is processed, then each value with an illegal type must be mapped\n    34→  // by exactly one of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\n    35→  // Values with a legal type may be mapped by ReplacedValues, but not by any of\n    36→  // the other maps.\n    37→\n    38→  // Note that these invariants may not hold momentarily when processing a node:\n    39→  // the node being processed may be put in a map before being marked Processed.\n    40→\n    41→  // Note that it is possible to have nodes marked NewNode in the DAG.  This can\n    42→  // occur in two ways.  Firstly, a node may be created during legalization but\n    43→  // never passed to the legalization core.  This is usually due to the implicit\n    44→  // folding that occurs when using the DAG.getNode operators.  Secondly, a new\n    45→  // node may be passed to the legalization core, but when analyzed may morph\n    46→  // into a different node, leaving the original node as a NewNode in the DAG.\n    47→  // A node may morph if one of its operands changes during analysis.  Whether\n    48→  // it actually morphs or not depends on whether, after updating its operands,\n    49→  // it is equivalent to an existing node: if so, it morphs into that existing\n    50→  // node (CSE).  An operand can change during analysis if the operand is a new\n    51→  // node that morphs, or it is a processed value that was mapped to some other\n    52→  // value (as recorded in ReplacedValues) in which case the operand is turned\n    53→  // into that other value.  If a node morphs then the node it morphed into will\n    54→  // be used instead of it for legalization, however the original node continues\n    55→  // to live on in the DAG.\n    56→  // The conclusion is that though there may be nodes marked NewNode in the DAG,\n    57→  // all uses of such nodes are also marked NewNode: the result is a fungus of\n    58→  // NewNodes growing on top of the useful nodes, and perhaps using them, but\n    59→  // not used by them.\n    60→\n    61→  // If a value is mapped by ReplacedValues, then it must have no uses, except\n    62→  // by nodes marked NewNode (see above).\n    63→\n    64→  // The final node obtained by mapping by ReplacedValues is not marked NewNode.\n    65→  // Note that ReplacedValues should be applied iteratively.\n    66→\n    67→  // Note that the ReplacedValues map may also map deleted nodes (by iterating\n    68→  // over the DAG we never dereference deleted nodes).  This means that it may\n    69→  // also map nodes marked NewNode if the deallocated memory was reallocated as\n    70→  // another node, and that new node was not seen by the LegalizeTypes machinery\n    71→  // (for example because it was created but not used).  In general, we cannot\n    72→  // distinguish between new nodes and deleted nodes.\n    73→  SmallVector<SDNode*, 16> NewNodes;\n    74→  for (SDNode &Node : DAG.allnodes()) {\n    75→    // Remember nodes marked NewNode - they are subject to extra checking below.\n    76→    if (Node.getNodeId() == NewNode)\n    77→      NewNodes.push_back(&Node);\n    78→\n    79→    for (unsigned i = 0, e = Node.getNumValues(); i != e; ++i) {\n    80→      SDValue Res(&Node, i);\n    81→      bool Failed = false;\n    82→      // Don't create a value in map.\n    83→      auto ResId = ValueToIdMap.lookup(Res);\n    84→\n    85→      unsigned Mapped = 0;\n    86→      if (ResId) {\n    87→        auto I = ReplacedValues.find(ResId);\n    88→        if (I != ReplacedValues.end()) {\n    89→          Mapped |= 1;\n    90→          // Check that remapped values are only used by nodes marked NewNode.\n    91→          for (SDUse &U : Node.uses())\n    92→            if (U.getResNo() == i)\n    93→              assert(U.getUser()->getNodeId() == NewNode &&\n    94→                     \"Remapped value has non-trivial use!\");\n    95→\n    96→          // Check that the final result of applying ReplacedValues is not\n    97→          // marked NewNode.\n    98→          auto NewValId = I->second;\n    99→          I = ReplacedValues.find(NewValId);\n   100→          while (I != ReplacedValues.end()) {\n   101→            NewValId = I->second;\n   102→            I = ReplacedValues.find(NewValId);\n   103→          }\n   104→          SDValue NewVal = getSDValue(NewValId);\n   105→          (void)NewVal;\n   106→          assert(NewVal.getNode()->getNodeId() != NewNode &&\n   107→                 \"ReplacedValues maps to a new node!\");\n   108→        }\n   109→        if (PromotedIntegers.count(ResId))\n   110→          Mapped |= 2;\n   111→        if (SoftenedFloats.count(ResId))\n   112→          Mapped |= 4;\n   113→        if (ScalarizedVectors.count(ResId))\n   114→          Mapped |= 8;\n   115→        if (ExpandedIntegers.count(ResId))\n   116→          Mapped |= 16;\n   117→        if (ExpandedFloats.count(ResId))\n   118→          Mapped |= 32;\n   119→        if (SplitVectors.count(ResId))\n   120→          Mapped |= 64;\n   121→        if (WidenedVectors.count(ResId))\n   122→          Mapped |= 128;\n   123→ It transforms\n// an arbitrary well-formed SelectionDAG to only consist of legal types.  This\n// is common code shared among the LegalizeTypes*.cpp files.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#include \"LegalizeTypes.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/SetVector.h\"\n#include \"llvm/IR/DataLayout.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/CommandLine.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/ErrorHandling.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/raw_ostream.h\"\nusing namespace llvm;\n\n#define DEBUG_TYPE \"legalize-types\"\n\nstatic cl::opt<bool>\nEnableExpensiveChecks(\"enable-legalize-types-checking\", cl::Hidden);\n\n/// Do extensive, expensive, basic correctness checking.\nvoid DAGTypeLegalizer::PerformExpensiveChecks() {\n  // If a node is not processed, then none of its values should be mapped by any\n  // of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\n\n  // If a node is processed, then each value with an illegal type must be mapped\n  // by exactly one of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\n  // Values with a legal type may be mapped by ReplacedValues, but not by any of\n  // the other maps.\n\n  // Note that these invariants may not hold momentarily when processing a node:\n  // the node being processed may be put in a map before being marked Processed.\n\n  // Note that it is possible to have nodes marked NewNode in the DAG.  This can\n  // occur in two ways.  Firstly, a node may be created during legalization but\n  // never passed to the legalization core.  This is usually due to the implicit\n  // folding that occurs when using the DAG.getNode operators.  Secondly, a new\n  // node may be passed to the legalization core, but when analyzed may morph\n  // into a different node, leaving the original node as a NewNode in the DAG.\n  // A node may morph if one of its operands changes during analysis.  Whether\n  // it actually morphs or not depends on whether, after updating its operands,\n  // it is equivalent to an existing node: if so, it morphs into that existing\n  // node (CSE).  An operand can change during analysis if the operand is a new\n  // node that morphs, or it is a processed value that was mapped to some other\n  // value (as recorded in ReplacedValues) in which case the operand is turned\n  // into that other value.  If a node morphs then the node it morphed into will\n  // be used instead of it for legalization, however the original node continues\n  // to live on in the DAG.\n  // The conclusion is that though there may be nodes marked NewNode in the DAG,\n  // all uses of such nodes are also marked NewNode: the result is a fungus of\n  // NewNodes growing on top of the useful nodes, and perhaps using them, but\n  // not used by them.\n\n  // If a value is mapped by ReplacedValues, then it must have no uses, except\n  // by nodes marked NewNode (see above).\n\n  // The final node obtained by mapping by ReplacedValues is not marked NewNode.\n  // Note that ReplacedValues should be applied iteratively.\n\n  // Note that the ReplacedValues map may also map deleted nodes (by iterating\n  // over the DAG we never dereference deleted nodes).  This means that it may\n  // also map nodes marked NewNode if the deallocated memory was reallocated as\n  // another node, and that new node was not seen by the LegalizeTypes machinery\n  // (for example because it was created but not used).  In general, we cannot\n  // distinguish between new nodes and deleted nodes.\n  SmallVector<SDNode*, 16> NewNodes;\n  for (SDNode &Node : DAG.allnodes()) {\n    // Remember nodes marked NewNode - they are subject to extra checking below.\n    if (Node.getNodeId() == NewNode)\n      NewNodes.push_back(&Node);\n\n    for (unsigned i = 0, e = Node.getNumValues(); i != e; ++i) {\n      SDValue Res(&Node, i);\n      bool Failed = false;\n      // Don't create a value in map.\n      auto ResId = ValueToIdMap.lookup(Res);\n\n      unsigned Mapped = 0;\n      if (ResId) {\n        auto I = ReplacedValues.find(ResId);\n        if (I != ReplacedValues.end()) {\n          Mapped |= 1;\n          // Check that remapped values are only used by nodes marked NewNode.\n          for (SDUse &U : Node.uses())\n            if (U.getResNo() == i)\n              assert(U.getUser()->getNodeId() == NewNode &&\n                     \"Remapped value has non-trivial use!\");\n\n          // Check that the final result of applying ReplacedValues is not\n          // marked NewNode.\n          auto NewValId = I->second;\n          I = ReplacedValues.find(NewValId);\n          while (I != ReplacedValues.end()) {\n            NewValId = I->second;\n            I = ReplacedValues.find(NewValId);\n          }\n          SDValue NewVal = getSDValue(NewValId);\n          (void)NewVal;\n          assert(NewVal.getNode()->getNodeId() != NewNode &&\n                 \"ReplacedValues maps to a new node!\");\n        }\n        if (PromotedIntegers.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 2;\n        if (SoftenedFloats.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 4;\n        if (ScalarizedVectors.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 8;\n        if (ExpandedIntegers.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 16;\n        if (ExpandedFloats.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 32;\n        if (SplitVectors.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 64;\n        if (WidenedVectors.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 128;\n        if (PromotedFloats.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 256;\n        if (SoftPromotedHalfs.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 512;\n      }\n\n      if (Node.getNodeId() != Processed) {\n        // Since we allow ReplacedValues to map deleted nodes, it may map nodes\n        // marked NewNode too, since a deleted node may have been reallocated as\n        // another node that has not been seen by the LegalizeTypes machinery.\n        if ((Node.getNodeId() == NewNode && Mapped > 1) ||\n            (Node.getNodeId() != NewNode && Mapped != 0)) {\n          dbgs() << \"Unprocessed value in a map!\";\n          Failed = true;\n        }\n      } else if (isTypeLegal(Res.getValueType()) || IgnoreNodeResults(&Node)) {\n        if (Mapped > 1) {\n          dbgs() << \"Value with legal type was transformed!\";\n          Failed = true;\n        }\n      } else {\n        if (Mapped == 0) {\n          SDValue NodeById = IdToValueMap.lookup(ResId);\n          // It is possible the node has been remapped to another node and had\n          // its Id updated in the Value to Id table. The node it remapped to\n          // may not have been processed yet. Look up the Id in the Id to Value\n          // table and re-check the Processed state. If the node hasn't been\n          // remapped we'll get the same state as we got earlier.","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":1048}}}

This allows the target specific behavior\n// of instructions to be described to target independent passes.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_CODEGEN_VALUETYPES_H\n#define LLVM_CODEGEN_VALUETYPES_H\n\n#include \"llvm/CodeGenTypes/MachineValueType.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/MathExtras.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/TypeSize.h\"\n#include <cassert>\n#include <cstdint>\n#include <string>\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\n  class LLVMContext;\n  class Type;\n  struct fltSemantics;\n\n  /// Extended Value Type. Capable of holding value types which are not native\n  /// for any processor (such as the i12345 type), as well as the types an MVT\n  /// can represent.\n  struct EVT {\n  private:\n    MVT V = MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE;\n    Type *LLVMTy = nullptr;\n\n  public:\n    constexpr EVT() = default;\n    constexpr EVT(MVT::SimpleValueType SVT) : V(SVT) {}\n    constexpr EVT(MVT S) : V(S) {}\n\n    bool operator==(EVT VT) const {\n      return !(*this != VT);\n    }\n    bool operator!=(EVT VT) const {\n      if (V.SimpleTy != VT.V.SimpleTy)\n        return true;\n      if (V.SimpleTy == MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n        return LLVMTy != VT.LLVMTy;\n      return false;\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the EVT that represents a floating-point type with the given\n    /// number of bits. There are two floating-point types with 128 bits - this\n    /// returns f128 rather than ppcf128.\n    static EVT getFloatingPointVT(unsigned BitWidth) {\n      return MVT::getFloatingPointVT(BitWidth);\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the EVT that represents an integer with the given number of\n    /// bits.\n    static EVT getIntegerVT(LLVMContext &Context, unsigned BitWidth) {\n      MVT M = MVT::getIntegerVT(BitWidth);\n      if (M.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n        return M;\n      return getExtendedIntegerVT(Context, BitWidth);\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the EVT that represents a vector NumElements in length, where\n    /// each element is of type VT.\n    static EVT getVectorVT(LLVMContext &Context, EVT VT, unsigned NumElements,\n                           bool IsScalable = false) {\n      MVT M = MVT::getVectorVT(VT.V, NumElements, IsScalable);\n      if (M.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n        return M;\n      return getExtendedVectorVT(Context, VT, NumElements, IsScalable);\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the EVT that represents a vector EC.Min elements in length,\n    /// where each element is of type VT.\n    static EVT getVectorVT(LLVMContext &Context, EVT VT, ElementCount EC) {\n      MVT M = MVT::getVectorVT(VT.V, EC);\n      if (M.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n        return M;\n      return getExtendedVectorVT(Context, VT, EC);\n    }\n\n    /// Return a vector with the same number of elements as this vector, but\n    /// with the element type converted to an integer type with the same\n    /// bitwidth.\n    EVT changeVectorElementTypeToInteger() const {\n      if (isSimple())\n        return getSimpleVT().changeVectorElementTypeToInteger();\n      return changeExtendedVectorElementTypeToInteger();\n    }\n\n    /// Return a VT for a vector type whose attributes match ourselves\n    /// with the exception of the element type that is chosen by the caller.\n    EVT changeVectorElementType(LLVMContext &Context, EVT EltVT) const {\n      if (isSimple() && EltVT.isSimple()) {\n        MVT M = MVT::getVectorVT(EltVT.getSimpleVT(), getVectorElementCount());\n        if (M != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n          return M;\n      }\n      return getVectorVT(Context, EltVT, getVectorElementCount());\n    }\n\n    /// Return a VT for a type whose attributes match ourselves with the\n    /// exception of the element type that is chosen by the caller.\n    EVT changeElementType(LLVMContext &Context, EVT EltVT) const {\n      EltVT = EltVT.getScalarType();\n      return isVector() ? changeVectorElementType(Context, EltVT) : EltVT;\n    }\n\n    /// Return the type converted to an equivalently sized integer or vector\n    /// with integer element type. Similar to changeVectorElementTypeToInteger,\n    /// but also handles scalars.\n    EVT changeTypeToInteger() const {\n      if (isVector())\n        return changeVectorElementTypeToInteger();\n\n      if (isSimple())\n        return getSimpleVT().changeTypeToInteger();\n      return changeExtendedTypeToInteger();\n    }\n\n    /// Test if the given EVT has zero size, this will fail if called on a\n    /// scalable type\n    bool isZeroSized() const {\n      return getSizeInBits().isZero();\n    }\n\n    /// Test if the given EVT is simple (as opposed to being extended).\n    bool isSimple() const {\n      return V.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE;\n    }\n\n    /// Test if the given EVT is extended (as opposed to being simple).\n    bool isExtended() const {\n      return !isSimple();\n    }\n\n    /// Return true if this is a FP or a vector FP type.\n    bool isFloatingPoint() const {\n      return isSimple() ? V.isFloatingPoint() : isExtendedFloatingPoint();\n    }\n","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":574}}}

IR Type System to Code Generation Flow\\n\\n## Type Creation and Class Hierarchy\\n\\nThe LLVM type system begins with the Type class hierarchy defined in llvm/include/llvm/IR/Type.h and llvm/include/llvm/IR/DerivedTypes.h:\\n\\n- **Type class** (Type.h, line 45): Base class for all LLVM types. Immutable and uniqued within an LLVMContext. Contains TypeID enum identifying the type category.\\n- **IntegerType** (DerivedTypes.h, line 42): Represents arbitrary-bit-width integers. Created via IntegerType::get(LLVMContext &C, unsigned NumBits), which ensures unique instances per bit width.\\n- **FunctionType** (DerivedTypes.h, line 105): Represents function signatures with return type and parameter types. Created via FunctionType::get(Type *Result, ArrayRef<Type*> Params, bool isVarArg).\\n- **StructType** (DerivedTypes.h, line 218): Represents structure types with named and unnamed variants. Created via StructType::get() for literal structs or StructType::create() for identified structs.\\n\\n## Type Context Ownership\\n\\nAll type instances are owned and uniqued by the LLVMContext through LLVMContextImpl (llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContextImpl.h and .cpp):\\n\\n- **LLVMContextImpl class**: Private implementation of LLVMContext. Every Type has a reference to the LLVMContext that created it (Type::Context member).\\n- **Type storage** (LLVMContextImpl.h, lines 1759-1776):\\n  - IntegerTypes: DenseMap<unsigned, IntegerType*> keyed by bit width\\n  - FunctionTypes: DenseSet<FunctionType*> using FunctionTypeKeyInfo for deduplication\\n  - AnonStructTypes: DenseSet<StructType*> for unnamed literal structs\\n  - NamedStructTypes: StringMap<StructType*> for identified structs\\n  - ArrayTypes: DenseMap<pair<Type*, uint64_t>, ArrayType*>\\n  - VectorTypes: DenseMap<pair<Type*, ElementCount>, VectorType*>\\n\\nThis design ensures single-instance semantics: only one IntegerType(i32) can exist per context, enabling pointer comparison for type equality.\\n\\n## IR Type Implementation\\n\\nThe Type.cpp file implements the Type class methods and provides type factory methods:\\n\\n- Type::getPrimitiveType(): Returns singleton primitive types (void, half, float, double, etc.)\\n- Type::getIntegerTy(), getFloatTy(), getDoubleTy(), etc.: Factory methods for primitive types\\n- Type property queries (isIntegerTy(), isFunctionTy(), isStructTy(), etc.)\\n\\n## IR to Machine Type Conversion\\n\\nThe conversion from LLVM IR types to machine/code generation types occurs through Extended Value Types (EVT):\\n\\n### EVT (Extended Value Type) - ValueTypes.h and ValueTypes.cpp\\n\\n- **EVT struct** (ValueTypes.h, line 35): Bridges IR types to machine types. Takes an IR Type* and returns EVT:\\n  - For IntegerType: Returns EVT created from bit width via getIntegerVT()\\n  - For VectorType: Recursively converts element type and wraps with getVectorVT()\\n  - For other types: Delegates to MVT::getVT()\\n- **EVT::getIntegerVT()** (ValueTypes.h, line 65-70): Creates or retrieves EVT for integer types\\n- **EVT::getVectorVT()** (ValueTypes.h, line 74-80): Creates EVT for vector types\\n\\n### MVT (Machine Value Type) - MachineValueType.h\\n\\n- **MVT class** (MachineValueType.h, line 36): Represents target-independent machine-level types.\\n- **SimpleValueType enum** (MachineValueType.h, line 38): Enumeration of all native processor types (i1, i8, i16, i32, i64, f32, f64, v4i32, etc.)\\n- MVT forms the base of EVT for standard types that map directly to native processor types.\\n\\n## Type Lowering in Code Generation\\n\\n### TargetLowering Type Conversion\\n\\nTargetLowering (include/llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h, lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/TargetLowering.cpp) provides target-specific type lowering:\\n\\n- **getValueType()** (TargetLowering.h, line 1740): Converts IR Type* to EVT, incorporating target-specific data layout:\\n  - Handles pointer types using target address spaces via getPointerTy()\\n  - Converts vector element types and reconstructs with getVectorVT()\\n  - Calls EVT::getEVT() for non-pointer types\\n- **getMemValueType()**: Memory-specific type conversion\\n- **getSimpleValueType()**: Converts Type* to MVT (returns simple value type only)\\n- **getTypeAction()**: Determines how illegal types should be legalized (TypeLegal, TypePromote, TypeSoften, TypeExpand, TypeSplitVector, TypeWidenVector)\\n\\n### SelectionDAG Builder\\n\\nThe SelectionDAGBuilder (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/SelectionDAGBuilder.h and .cpp) converts LLVM IR to SelectionDAG:\\n\\n- **Translates IR instructions to SDNodes**: Each IR value becomes an SDValue with an EVT\\n- Uses TargetLowering::getValueType() to determine node value types\\n- Maps IR types to machine types during IR-to-DAG conversion\\n- Handles complex type splitting and promotion inline\\n\\n### Type Legalization Pipeline\\n\\nOnce SelectionDAG is built with EVTs, the LegalizeTypes pass (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/) transforms illegal types to legal ones:\\n\\n**DAGTypeLegalizer class** (LegalizeTypes.h and .cpp):\\n- Walks SelectionDAG and legalizes all node value types\\n- Uses TargetLowering::getTypeAction() to determine legalization strategy\\n- Maintains multiple remapping maps **SplitVectors**: Large vectors split into smaller vectors\\n  - **WidenedVectors**: Small vectors widened to legal sizes\\n\\n**Type-specific legalization** is implemented across multiple files:\\n- **LegalizeIntegerTypes.cpp**: Promotes, expands, or converts integer types\\n- **LegalizeFloatTypes.cpp**: Softens, promotes, or expands FP types\\n- **LegalizeVectorTypes.cpp**: Scalarizes, splits, or widens vector types\\n- **LegalizeTypesGeneric.cpp**: Generic legalization for complex operations\\n- **LegalizeDAG.cpp**: DAG-level operation legalization post-type legalization\\n\\n## Complete Type Flow\\n\\n1. **IR Creation**: User code creates Type instances via Type::getIntNTy(), IntegerType::get(), FunctionType::get(), StructType::get()\\n2. **Context Ownership**: LLVMContextImpl stores and deduplicates all types, ensuring type equality via pointer comparison\\n3. **IR to SelectionDAG**: SelectionDAGBuilder converts IR values to SDNodes, obtaining EVT via LLVM type system begins with the Type class hierarchy defined in llvm/include/llvm/IR/Type.h and llvm/include/llvm/IR/DerivedTypes.h:\\n\\n- **Type class** (Type.h, line 45): Base class for all LLVM types. Immutable and uniqued within an LLVMContext. Contains TypeID enum identifying the type category.\\n- **IntegerType** (DerivedTypes.h, line 42): Represents arbitrary-bit-width integers. Created via IntegerType::get(LLVMContext &C, unsigned NumBits), which ensures unique instances per bit width.\\n- **FunctionType** (DerivedTypes.h, line 105): Represents function signatures with return type and parameter types. Created via FunctionType::get(Type *Result, ArrayRef<Type*> Params, bool isVarArg).\\n- **StructType** (DerivedTypes.h, line 218): Represents structure types with named and unnamed variants. Created via StructType::get() for literal structs or StructType::create() for identified structs.\\n\\n## Type Context Ownership\\n\\nAll type instances are owned and uniqued by the LLVMContext through LLVMContextImpl (llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContextImpl.h and .cpp):\\n\\n- **LLVMContextImpl class**: Private implementation of LLVMContext. Every Type has a reference to the LLVMContext that created it (Type::Context member).\\n- **Type storage** (LLVMContextImpl.h, lines 1759-1776):\\n  - IntegerTypes: DenseMap<unsigned, IntegerType*> keyed by bit width\\n  - FunctionTypes: DenseSet<FunctionType*> using FunctionTypeKeyInfo for deduplication\\n  - AnonStructTypes: DenseSet<StructType*> for unnamed literal structs\\n  - NamedStructTypes: StringMap<StructType*> for identified structs\\n  - ArrayTypes: DenseMap<pair<Type*, uint64_t>, ArrayType*>\\n  - VectorTypes: DenseMap<pair<Type*, ElementCount>, VectorType*>\\n\\nThis design ensures single-instance semantics: only one IntegerType(i32) can exist per context, enabling pointer comparison for type equality.\\n\\n## IR Type Implementation\\n\\nThe Type.cpp file implements the Type class methods and provides type factory methods:\\n\\n- Type::getPrimitiveType(): Returns singleton primitive types (void, half, float, double, etc.)\\n- Type::getIntegerTy(), getFloatTy(), getDoubleTy(), etc.: Factory methods for primitive types\\n- Type property queries (isIntegerTy(), isFunctionTy(), isStructTy(), etc.)\\n\\n## IR to Machine Type Conversion\\n\\nThe conversion from LLVM IR types to machine/code generation types occurs through Extended Value Types (EVT):\\n\\n### EVT (Extended Value Type) - ValueTypes.h and ValueTypes.cpp\\n\\n- **EVT struct** (ValueTypes.h, line 35): Bridges IR types to machine types. Contains an MVT (simple value type) and optionally an LLVM Type* for non-standard types.\\n- **EVT::getEVT()** (ValueTypes.cpp, line 301): Main conversion function. Takes an IR Type* and returns EVT:\\n  - For IntegerType: Returns EVT created from bit width via getIntegerVT()\\n  - For VectorType: Recursively converts element type and wraps with getVectorVT()\\n  - For other types: Delegates to MVT::getVT()\\n- **EVT::getIntegerVT()** (ValueTypes.h, line 65-70): Creates or retrieves EVT for integer types\\n- **EVT::getVectorVT()** (ValueTypes.h, line 74-80): Creates EVT for vector types\\n\\n### MVT (Machine Value Type) - MachineValueType.h\\n\\n- **MVT class** (MachineValueType.h, line 36): Represents target-independent machine-level types.\\n- **SimpleValueType enum** (MachineValueType.h, line 38): Enumeration of all native processor types (i1, i8, i16, i32, i64, f32, f64, v4i32, etc.)\\n- MVT forms the base of EVT for standard types that map directly to native processor types.\\n\\n## Type Lowering in Code Generation\\n\\n### TargetLowering Type Conversion\\n\\nTargetLowering (include/llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h, lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/TargetLowering.cpp) provides target-specific type lowering:\\n\\n- **getValueType()** (TargetLowering.h, line 1740): Converts IR Type* to EVT, incorporating target-specific data layout:\\n  - Handles pointer types using target address spaces via getPointerTy()\\n  - Converts vector element types and reconstructs with getVectorVT()\\n  - Calls EVT::getEVT() for non-pointer types\\n- **getMemValueType()**: Memory-specific type conversion\\n- **getSimpleValueType()**: Converts Type* to MVT (returns simple value type only)\\n- **getTypeAction()**: Determines how illegal types should be legalized (TypeLegal, TypePromote, TypeSoften, TypeExpand, TypeSplitVector, TypeWidenVector)\\n\\n### SelectionDAG Builder\\n\\nThe SelectionDAGBuilder (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/SelectionDAGBuilder.h and .cpp) converts LLVM IR to SelectionDAG:\\n\\n- **Translates IR instructions to SDNodes**: Each IR value becomes an SDValue with an EVT\\n- Uses TargetLowering::getValueType() to determine node value types\\n- Maps IR types to machine types during IR-to-DAG conversion\\n- Handles complex type splitting and promotion inline\\n\\n### Type Legalization Pipeline\\n\\nOnce SelectionDAG is built with EVTs, the LegalizeTypes pass (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/) transforms illegal types to legal ones:\\n\\n**DAGTypeLegalizer class** (LegalizeTypes.h and .cpp):\\n- Walks SelectionDAG and legalizes all node value types\\n- Uses TargetLowering::getTypeAction() to determine legalization strategy\\n- Maintains multiple remapping maps for different legalization kinds:\\n  - **PromotedIntegers**: Small integers promoted to legal sizes\\n  - **ExpandedIntegers**: Large integers split into smaller parts\\n  - **SoftenedFloats**: Floating point converted to integer representation\\n  - **PromotedFloats**: Small FP types promoted to legal sizes\\n  - **ScalarizedVectors**: Single-element vectors converted to scalars\\n  - **SplitVectors**: Large vectors split into smaller vectors\\n  - **WidenedVectors**: Small vectors widened to legal sizes\\n\\n**Type-specific legalization** is implemented across multiple files:\\n- **LegalizeIntegerTypes.cpp**: Promotes, expands, or converts integer types\\n- **LegalizeFloatTypes.cpp**: Softens, promotes, or expands FP types\\n- **LegalizeVectorTypes.cpp**: Scalarizes, splits, or widens vector types\\n- **LegalizeTypesGeneric.cpp**: Generic legalization for complex operations\\n- **LegalizeDAG.cpp**: DAG-level operation legalization post-type legalization\\n\\n## Complete Type Flow\\n\\n1. **IR Creation**: User code creates Type instances via Type::getIntNTy(), IntegerType::get(), FunctionType::get(), StructType::get()\\n2. **Context Ownership**: LLVMContextImpl stores and deduplicates all types, ensuring type equality via pointer comparison\\n3. **IR to SelectionDAG**: SelectionDAGBuilder converts IR values to SDNodes, obtaining EVT via target-legal types using TargetLowering type action information\\n6. **Final Lowering**: Legalized SDDAGs are lowered to machine code with only legal MVT types\\n\\nThis architecture ensures a clean separation between IR-level type semantics (Type hierarchy) and code generation type constraints (EVT/MVT and legalization), with LLVMContext/LLVMContextImpl managing type uniqueness and ownership
